## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This is a nonlinear harmonic oscillator problem where acceleration (dv_dt) depends on position, velocity, and possibly time. The equation of motion encodes restoring forces (functions of x), damping (functions of v), and possibly external driving (functions of t).

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Linear harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (restoring force with linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator (unforced): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Duffing with damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic spring with linear damping)
- Duffing with quintic: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 + c3 * v (higher-order nonlinear spring)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (forced nonlinear oscillator)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x * abs(x) (asymmetric nonlinear restoring force)
- Nonlinear damping with cubic spring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * v**3 (nonlinear spring and damping)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (asymmetric restoring force)
- Mixed nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v (general polynomial restoring force with damping)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * cos(c1 * t) (time-modulated stiffness)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (velocity-dependent nonlinear damping)
- Driven damped linear: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (driven linear oscillator)
- Coulomb-damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (v**2)**(-0.5) * v (friction-like damping, sign-dependent)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) preserve symmetry of oscillation; even powers (x²) break symmetry → use odd polynomials in x for symmetric oscillators
- Velocity-dependent terms with position modulation like (1 - x²)*v indicate self-sustained oscillations (limit cycles) as in Van der Pol systems
- Cubic position terms x³ with same/opposite sign as linear term x indicate hardening/softening spring behavior respectively
- Periodic driving forces appear as sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) and are the only way explicit time dependence typically enters oscillator equations
- Nonlinear damping (v³ or v*|v|) becomes important at high velocities and produces amplitude-dependent energy dissipation
- Products x*v indicate phase-space coupling and can arise from coordinate transformations or nonlinear energy exchange mechanisms
- Absence of explicit time dependence suggests an autonomous system where energy is either conserved or dissipated but not externally supplied
- Square root of sum of squares sqrt(x² + v²) represents amplitude in phase space and appears in amplitude-dependent nonlinearities
